> **Follow-up Report 1 of 6** (added 2026-06-24) · `2026-06-22_CT_WB-FDG-PET-CT-scan.md`

# WB FDG PET - CT scan (follow-up)

- **Date performed**: 2026-06-22
- **Category**: CT
- **Facility**: Prismaa Oncoimaging, Surat
- **Referred by**: Dr. Kaushal B. Patel (MD, DM Medical Oncology)
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-06-22_CT_WB-FDG-PET-CT-scan.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-06-22_CT_WB-FDG-PET-CT-scan.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `SAROJ AGRAWAL - New PET Scan June 2026.pdf`
- **Compared with**: prior PET-CT dated 2026-02-21 (report 23.02.2026), Sir H. N. Reliance Foundation Hospital

## Summary (extracted)

18 F-FDG Whole Body Digital PET-CT Study. 5.38 mCi 18F-FDG injected after 5–6 hrs fasting;
AI-assisted 160-slice digital PET-CT acquired 60 min post-injection; separate breath-hold CT;
extent vertex to mid-thigh.

**Referral reasons**: Known case of Ca. endometrium with lung metastasis. Post immuno- and
chemotherapy (last dose 15/06/2026). Complaints of breathing difficulty on and off. For
follow-up evaluation. (History noted: NT-proBNP 1738 high & CPK-MB 34.67 high on 11/02/2026,
Troponin-I negative; CA-125 635.50 on 14/02/2026; pleural fluid cytology — atypical cells
suggestive of carcinoma with large cell morphology, 14/02/2026.)

### Findings
- **Brain**: Physiological FDG distribution, no focal hypermetabolic lesion. No intracranial
  metastatic disease.
- **Head & Neck**: Previously noted metabolically active necrotic left cervical nodal disease
  shows **marked interval regression**. Residual left level V cervical node ≈ **12 × 8 mm,
  SUVmax 3.19** (previously 20 × 24 mm, SUVmax 12.7). Mild diffuse thyroid uptake, likely
  inflammatory. No new metabolically active cervical lymphadenopathy.
- **Chest**: **Interval significant reduction in bilateral pleural disease** — now mild
  residual bilateral pleural effusions, greater on the left. Right pleural hypermetabolic
  thickening regressed, residual low-grade **SUVmax 5.4** (previously 5.6). No focal FDG-avid
  pulmonary parenchymal lesion. Mild bibasal compressive atelectasis. Mediastinal nodal disease
  **markedly regressed** — tiny residual prevascular node ≈ 8 × 7 mm, SUVmax 4.93; tiny right
  upper paratracheal nodes low-grade. No significant FDG-avid hilar lymphadenopathy. Bilateral
  axillary nodes small, low-grade, likely stable. No pericardial effusion. **No residual
  pulmonary arterial thrombus** on the CT component.
- **Abdomen & Pelvis**: Post-hysterectomy status; no abnormal FDG at the operative bed.
  **Significant interval regression of omental and peritoneal metastatic disease** — residual
  tiny metabolically active peritoneal/omental nodule ≈ **8.5 × 6.8 mm, SUVmax 7.12**;
  previously extensive supramesocolic omental nodularity no longer measurable. Mild residual
  ascites. Calcified bilateral common iliac nodes without significant activity. Abdominal nodal
  disease substantially regressed. Left inguinal node now ≈ **17 × 10 mm, SUVmax 2.85**
  (previously 23 × 14 mm, SUVmax 6.4). Multiple simple hepatic cysts (largest segment VI,
  3.2 cm); small calcified granuloma segment III; **no FDG-avid hepatic metastasis**. Spleen,
  pancreas, adrenals, kidneys normal. Mild subcutaneous edema of lower anterior pelvic wall.
- **Musculoskeletal**: **No FDG-avid osseous metastatic lesion.** Mild degenerative spondylotic
  changes.

### Conclusion (vs prior PET-CT 23.02.2026)
1. Marked interval regression of left cervical metastatic lymphadenopathy (residual left level V
   node 12 × 8 mm, SUVmax 3.19, prev 20 × 24 mm, SUVmax 12.7).
2. Significant regression of mediastinal, axillary, infraclavicular, abdominal and
   inguinofemoral nodal disease — only small residual mildly FDG-avid nodes.
3. Significant regression of peritoneal carcinomatosis and omental deposits — only tiny residual
   metabolically active peritoneal nodule (8.5 × 6.8 mm, SUVmax 7.12).
4. Interval reduction in bilateral malignant pleural disease — persistent mild bilateral pleural
   effusions and mild residual pleural FDG uptake (SUVmax 5.4).
5. Mild residual ascites.

### RECIST 1.1 Assessment
- Target lesions:
  - Left level V cervical node: 20 mm → 8 mm (short axis)
  - Left inguinal node: 14 mm → 10 mm (short axis)
- Sum of target lesion diameters: **Previous 34 mm → Current 18 mm**
- Non-target: pleural disease improved; omental/peritoneal near-complete regression; mediastinal
  & abdominal nodal disease significantly regressed without appreciable residual FDG avidity.
- **Percentage change: −47.1%**
- **RECIST 1.1 overall response: PARTIAL RESPONSE (PR)**
- Overall: significant favourable treatment response with marked reduction in nodal, pleural and
  peritoneal metastatic disease burden; residual metabolically active disease as described.

### Reporting doctors
Dr. Manas Mayank (MD, DRM — Consultant Nuclear Medicine); Dr. Shubham Padashetty (MBBS, MD —
Consultant Onco-Radiologist); Dr. Krishan Kant Agarwal (MBBS, MD — Consultant & Nuclear
Medicine); Dr. Keyur Mandaliya (MBBS, DNB — Consultant Onco-Radiologist).

# Combined Panel — CBC + Electrolytes + Creatinine + NT-proBNP + LFT (Surat, Nobel Micropath)

- **Date performed**: 2026-06-15
- **Category**: Lab-Surat
- **Lab**: Nobel Micropath Laboratory, Surat (NABL MC-7707)
- **Referring doctor**: Dr. Kaushal Patel (MD, DM Oncology)
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-06-15_Lab-Surat_Combined-Panel.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-06-15_Lab-Surat_Combined-Panel.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `606102844.pdf` (lab registration no.)

## Summary (extracted)

Bundled outpatient panel collected 15/06/2026 09:27 AM at Nobel Micropath, Surat.

**CBC (EDTA Whole Blood):** Hb **10.9 g/dL (LOW; ref 11.0–15.0)**, HCT **34.70 % (LOW; ref 36.0–46.0)**, RBC **3.44 × 10⁶/cmm (LOW; ref 3.8–4.8)**, MCV **100.9 fL (HIGH; ref 83–101)**, MCH 31.7 pg (normal), **MCHC 31.4 % (LOW; ref 31.5–34.5)**, **RDW 16.9 % (HIGH; ref 11.6–14.0)**, **WBC 12170/cmm (HIGH; ref 4000–10000)**. Differential: Neut 69 % (ANC 8397), Lymph 22 % (2677), Eos 1 % (122), Mono 8 % (974), Baso 0 %. Platelets 251000/cmm (normal). MPV 9.3 fL. Peripheral smear: anisocytosis (+); **leucocytosis**; platelets adequate; no malarial parasites.

**Electrolytes (Serum, ISE):** Sodium 139, Potassium 4.7, Chloride 104 mmol/L — all **normal**.

**Creatinine (Serum, Jaffe):** 0.93 mg/dL — **normal** (ref 0.6–1.1).

**NT-proBNP (CLIA):** **97.2 pg/mL — normal** (ref 0–531; heart failure unlikely).

**Liver Function Test (Serum):** SGPT 13.9 U/L, SGOT 13.00 U/L, ALP 73.2 U/L, Total Bilirubin 0.2, Conjugated 0.1, Unconjugated 0.1, GGT 18.3, A/G ratio 1.45 — all **normal**. **Albumin 3.26 g/dL — now NORMAL (ref 3.2–4.6)**. Still mildly low: **Total Protein 5.51 g/dL (ref 6.4–8.0)**, **Globulin 2.25 g/dL (ref 2.3–3.5)**.

**Findings**: Clear interval improvement vs the May labs. **Haemoglobin has risen 8.4 → 9.7 → 9.7 → 10.3 → 10.9 g/dL (06 May → 15 Jun)** — anaemia improving though still mildly low and macrocytic (MCV 100.9, high RDW). **Albumin has normalised (2.65 → 3.26)** and total protein is up (4.62 → 5.51), so the hypoproteinaemia driving earlier edema is largely corrected. **NT-proBNP 97.2 (normal)** — a major improvement from 1738 (high) in February, indicating no current cardiac strain/failure. Renal function preserved; creatinine 0.71 → 0.93 over six weeks (still normal, mild upward trend worth watching). New finding: **mild neutrophilic leucocytosis (WBC 12170, ANC 8397)** — likely reactive (post-chemo/steroid/inflammatory); correlate clinically.

# Combined Panel — CBC + Electrolytes + Creatinine + LFT (Surat, Nobel Micropath)

- **Date performed**: 2026-05-06
- **Category**: Lab-Surat
- **Lab**: Nobel Micropath Laboratory, Surat (NABL MC-7707)
- **Referring doctor**: Dr. Kaushal Patel (MD, DM Oncology)
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-05-06_Lab-Surat_Combined-Panel.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-05-06_Lab-Surat_Combined-Panel.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `605100986.pdf` (lab registration no.)

## Summary (extracted)

Bundled outpatient panel collected 06/05/2026 10:05 AM at Nobel Micropath, Surat.

**CBC (EDTA Whole Blood):** Hb **8.4 g/dL (LOW; ref 11.0–15.0)**, HCT **26.5 % (LOW; ref 36.0–46.0)**, RBC **2.79 × 10⁶/cmm (LOW; ref 3.8–4.8)**, MCV 95.0 fL (normal), MCH 30.1 pg (normal), MCHC 31.7 % (normal), **RDW 21.4 % (HIGH; ref 11.6–14.0)**, WBC 5410/cmm (normal). Differential: Neut 53 % (ANC 2867), Lymph 34 % (1839), Eos 1 % (54), Mono 12 % (649; borderline-high), Baso 0 %. Platelets 352000/cmm (normal). MPV 9.3 fL. Peripheral smear: anisocytosis (+); WBCs/platelets within normal limits; no malarial parasites.

**Electrolytes (Serum, ISE):** Sodium 139, Potassium 4.3, Chloride 103 mmol/L — all **normal**.

**Creatinine (Serum, Jaffe):** 0.71 mg/dL — **normal** (ref 0.6–1.1).

**Liver Function Test (Serum):** SGPT 6.7 U/L, SGOT 11.9 U/L, ALP 71.2 U/L, Total Bilirubin 0.2, Conjugated 0.1, Unconjugated 0.1, GGT 16.2 — all **normal**. However, **Total Protein 4.62 g/dL (LOW; ref 6.4–8.0)**, **Albumin 2.65 g/dL (LOW; ref 3.2–4.6)**, **Globulin 1.97 g/dL (LOW; ref 2.3–3.5)**, A/G ratio 1.35 (normal).

**Findings**: Persistent normochromic-macrocytic anaemia (Hb 8.4, MCV high-normal, elevated RDW = mixed cause / nutritional + chemo-marrow effects). Liver enzymes fully normal. **Marked hypoproteinemia / hypoalbuminemia (Albumin 2.65)** continues from the April labs and is the likely driver of the new bilateral leg / abdominal edema being clinically observed. Renal function and electrolytes preserved.

> **Follow-up Report 6 of 6** (added 2026-06-24) · `2026-05-01_USG_Right-Lower-Limb-Arterial-Venous-Doppler.md`

# Right Lower Extremity Arterial & Venous Doppler Study (Surat, Navkar)

- **Date performed**: 2026-05-01
- **Category**: USG
- **Centre**: Navkar Radio Diagnostic Center, Surat (Vesu / Althan)
- **Referring doctor**: Dr. Sanjay Agrawal
- **Reported by**: Dr. Jenish Shah (MBBS, MD Radiologist); Dr. Parth Bhut (DNB Radiodiagnosis)
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-05-01_USG_Right-Lower-Limb-Arterial-Venous-Doppler.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-05-01_USG_Right-Lower-Limb-Arterial-Venous-Doppler.pdf)
- **Image plates (companion PDF)**: [`./report_pdf/2026-05-01_USG_Right-Lower-Limb-Arterial-Venous-Doppler_images.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-05-01_USG_Right-Lower-Limb-Arterial-Venous-Doppler_images.pdf)
- **Original filenames**: `093212_SAROJ AGARWAL.pdf` (report) + `093212_SAROJ AGARWAL_01May26_113935_000.pdf` (images)

## Summary (extracted)

Real-time colour-flow and pulsed-Doppler study of the arterial & venous drainage of the **right lower limb**, done 01/05/2026 at Navkar, Surat (for evaluation of right-leg swelling).

**Key result — NO DVT.** No signs of acute or chronic thrombosis in the arterial or venous system; no haemodynamically significant stenosis or occlusion; no superficial vein thrombosis or abnormal perforators; veins compressible with normal augmentation (++) and normal phasic flow.

**Arterial**: Common femoral, superficial femoral, popliteal, anterior tibial, posterior tibial and peroneal arteries normal in course and calibre, with normal triphasic waveforms and normal colour filling (incl. dorsalis pedis). **Mild atheromatous plaque & intimo-medial thickening** noted. No abnormal arterial occlusion.

**Venous**: Common femoral, superficial femoral, deep femoral, popliteal, anterior tibial and posterior tibial veins normal; probe-compressible; normal colour filling; sapheno-femoral junction normal flow direction. No greater/short saphenous varicosities.

**Soft tissue (explains the swelling)**: Moderate-to-severe subcutaneous fat-plane oedema of the **right leg / ankle / foot**; minimal-to-mild superficial subcutaneous fat-plane inhomogeneous echogenicity throughout the right thigh — possible **subtle superficial haemorrhage / petechial sequelae** (in keeping with anticoagulation). No abnormal focal lesion or collection.

**Clinical significance**: The right-leg swelling is due to subcutaneous oedema (± petechial haemorrhage sequelae), **not DVT** — reassuring given her prior saddle pulmonary embolism and ongoing anticoagulation.

```
Urea:
Urea is the final degradation product of protein and amino acid metabolism. Blood urea nitrogen currently is the most widely
used screening test for the evaluation of kidney function. Protein catabolism causes formation of ammonia which is
synthesized to urea with and elimination of excess nitrogen in the liver. Increased blood urea nitrogen may be due to cardiac
decompensation, water depletion due to decreased intake and excessive loss, increased protein catabolism, high protein
diet, acute glomerulonephritis, chronic nephritis, polycystic kidney disease, nephrosclerosis, tubular necrosis and all types of
obstruction of the urinary tract.
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. ARCHI CHAWLA DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry M.D Pathology M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
Consultant Biochemist Clinical Assistant Consultant Pathologist
```

```
Total Bilirubin:
• Diseases or conditions which, through hemolytic processes, produce bilirubin faster than the liver can metabolize it,
cause the levels of unconjugated (indirect) bilirubin to increase in the circulation.
• Liver immaturity and several other diseases in which the bilirubin conjugation mechanism is impaired cause similar
elevations of circulating unconjugated bilirubin.
• Bile duct obstruction or damage to hepatocellular structure causes increases in the levels of both conjugated (direct)
and unconjugated (indirect)bilirubin in the circulation.
```

# Discharge Summary

- **Date performed**: 2026-04-08
- **Category**: Summary-Discharge
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-04-08_Summary-Discharge_Discharge-Summary.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-04-08_Summary-Discharge_Discharge-Summary.pdf)

## Summary (extracted)

Inpatient Discharge Summary — Case Number 1003707451. Admission: Feb 20, 2026 03:36 AM; Discharge: Apr 8, 2026 01:38 PM. Attending: Dr. Darshit Shah (Medical Oncology). Diagnosis: Ca Uterus (C54). Presenting complaints: transferred from outside hospital with breathlessness, cough, bilateral pedal edema; CXR showed left pleural effusion; ICD in situ since 12/02/2026; pleural fluid showed atypical cells (?large cell morphology); H/O Ca Uterus operated 3 years back. Hospital course (highlights): Severe pulmonary hypertension (PASP ~78 mmHg) with LVEF 60%; left vocal cord lateralisation performed 26.02.2026 due to bilateral vocal cord palsy with restricted mobility (post-op required intubation, ICU admission). Multiple cycles of chemotherapy (Paclitaxel + Carboplatin +/- Dostarlimab) administered C1D1 20.02.2026, C1D8 02.03.2026, and C3D1 06.04.2026. Episodes of polymorphic PVCs/VTach managed with Xylocard, Cordarone, Mexiletine. Saddle submassive pulmonary embolism diagnosed 25.03.2026 on CTPA — managed with Clexane anticoagulation, oxygen, vasopressors. Mild hemoptysis, transfusions provided. Sputum showed budding yeast/pseudohyphae (fungal); right lobe consolidation; broad-spectrum antibiotics (Zavicefta, Aztreonam, Augmentin), antifungals administered. FEES study — improved vocal cord approximation, no overt aspiration; pleasure pureed diet only. Procedures listed: Echocardiography Portable, WB FDG PET CECT scan, Rehab med-chest therapy (x2), USG Portable Kidney/Transplant Kidney/KUB, X Ray Portable Chest AP. Condition at discharge: hemodynamically stable. Discharge medications: Pan 40mg, Emeset 8mg, Clexane 0.6ml SC BD x14d then Apixaban 5mg BD, Cordarone 200, Aldactone 50, Mexohar 150, Tadalafil 20mg, Foracort/Duolin nebs, Effcorlin 50mg IV TDS x3d, Augmentin 1.2g IV BD x3d. Follow-up with Dr. Darshit Shah for next chemo C3D8 on 13/4/2026; OPD with Dr. Sushil Bidroo on 13/04/2026 with chest X-ray.

```
immunotherapy and chemotherapy, and the patient was advised to continue pleasure feeds.
Supportive care with IV fluids and multivitamins administered.
```

The gastro-esophageal junction is normal.

aspiration.
Incidental note is made of patchy consolidates in the right upper zone and both midzones.

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Creatinine:
```

```
fields

fields
10-99 AFB per 100 oil 100 1+ Positive
immersion fields
1-10 AFB per oil immersion field 50 2+ Positive
More than 10 AFB per oil 20 3+ Positive
Immersion field

antibiotics tested by Kirby Bauer’s method and MIC value is not reported for antibiotics which are deduced by software as per CLSI Guidelines. Colistin MIC
is tested by Microbroth Dilution method.
Remarks:
• Results of culture and antimicrobial susceptibility test needs to be correlate clinically.
• Previous history of antibiotic usage may influence the growth of microorganisms in vitro.
• Result is dependent on the quality of specimen submitted.
• Smear-positivity and grade indicates relative bacterial burden.
• Changes in smear status important for monitoring response to therapy.
• Kindly note AFB stain does not distinguish between viable and dead organisms nor differentiates species of Mycobacteria.
• Mycobacteria Genxpert and MTB automated culture recommended if clinically indicated.
• A negative AFB smear may mean that no infection is present, that symptoms are caused by some other microorganism, or that the mycobacteria
were not present in sufficient numbers to be seen under the microscope.
```

```
Test Name Result
Method/ Principle of BacTAlert Virtuo analyser: BacT/ALERT Virtuo Microbial Detection Systems utilize a colorimetric
sensor and reflected light to monitor the presence and production of carbon dioxide (CO2) that is dissolved in the culture
medium. If microorganisms are present in the test sample, carbon dioxide is produced as the organisms metabolize the
substrates in the culture medium. When growth of the microorganisms produces CO2, the color of the gas-permeable sensor
installed in the bottom of each culture bottle changes to yellow. Neutralizes all classes of antibiotics by FAN Plus method that
normally hinder growth in manual blood culture methods.
Positive flagged cultures are processed on culture media. Identification by automated MALDITOF/Vitek 2 and or conventional
methods, sensitivity on vitek 2. Certain antibiotics tested by Kirby Bauer’s method and MIC is not reported for antibiotics
which are deduced by software as per CLSI. Antisera tested as and when applicable.
Remark:
1. Results of culture and antimicrobial susceptibility test needs to be correlate clinically.
2. Previous history of antibiotic usage may influence the growth of microorganisms in vitro.
Colony Count Interpretation
Colony Counts of 10000 to >= 100000 CFU/ml Significant uropathogen. Suggestive of Urinary
of single/two Potential pathogen/s. tract infection (UTI) needs treatment based on
antimicrobial susceptibility test results.
Colony counts between 1000 to 10000 Can be considered Significant growth,
CFU/ml of single Potential pathogen. correlation with Microscopy and Clinical
history required.
Colony counts between 100 to1000 CFU/ml. Insignificant growth. Probable commensal
contamination during voiding.
Either two or three organism types with Suggestive of Urinary tract infection (UTI)
predominant growth of one organism type and needs treatment based on antimicrobial
<10000CFU/mL of the other organism type(s) susceptibility test results. Correlation with
Microscopy and clinical history required
Any number / Any count. Significant in case of Suprapubic
aspirates/surgically obtained (e.g. cystoscopy)
urine specimens.
>= 3 organism types with no predominant Fresh specimen required as possibility of
(10000 >= 100000 CFU/ml) pathogen. contamination during voiding.
∞ End of Report ∞
DR. NEETU BIYANI DR. SHASHIKALA SHIVAPRAKASHA
MD Microbiology MD Microbiology
```

```
Venous Blood Gas Analysis:
• Analysis of arterial and mixed venous blood provides information concerning the oxygenation, ventilatory, and acid-
base status of the patient from whom the specimen was obtained.
• Analysis of samples from other sources (ie, capillary, peripheral venous, umbilical venous samples, and pH
measured from other body fluids) may provide limited information. The variables most generally measured are the
PaCO2, PaO2, and pH.
• While there is some evidence that venous and arterial pH, PCO2, and HCO3 may have sufficient agreement as to be
clinically comparable in a variety of clinical settings, the venous blood gas (VBG) obtained from a central line should
be considered a surrogate for arterial blood gas (ABG) only in very specific clinical circumstances.
Reference:
• AARC Clinical Practice Guideline: Blood Gas Analysis and Hemoximetry: 2013
• Michael D Davis, Brian K Walsh, Steve E Sittig and Ruben D Restrepo
• Respiratory Care October 2013, 58 (10) 1694-1703
∞ End of Report ∞
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. RINA SHAH DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry M.D Pathology M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Creatinine:
Creatinine is synthesized endogenously from creatine and creatine phosphate and is removed from plasma by glomerular
```

```
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Procalcitonin Quantitative
ng/mL <= 0.15 0.65
(Serum,CMIA/Electrochemiluminescence)
Procalcitonin Quantitative:
1. Procalcitonin (PCT) is an amino acid precursor of calcitonin peptide. PCT becomes detectable within 2 to 4 hours after a
triggering event and peaks by 12 to 24 hours. PCT secretion parallels closely the severity of the inflammatory insult, with
higher levels associated with more severe disease and declining levels with resolution of illness.
2. During severe systemic inflammation, especially related to bacterial infection, PCT and CCP-1 are secreted in large
quantities. Noninfectious inflammatory stimuli need to be extremely severe to result in PCT elevations, making it a more
specific marker for severe infections. In the absence of an ongoing stimulus. It it suitable for serial monitoring.
3. Reported results are for the information of the referring Clinician. Results should be interpreted in correlation with medical
history, clinical presentation and other findings.
4. Reference ranges and clinical information/interpretations are traceable to kit inserts/textbooks/defined guidelines.
∞ End of Report ∞
DDRR.. KKSSHHAAMMAA PPIIMMPPAALLGGAAOONNKKAARR DR. RINA SHAH DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
MM DD BBiioocchheemmiissttrryy M.D Pathology M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
```

```
Test performed on Fully Automated Coagulometer.
Prothrombin Time (PT):
• Prothrombin time (PT) is used to evaluate the extrinsic and common pathways of coagulation, which helps detect
deficiencies of factors ( II, V, VII, X ) and low fibrinogen concentrations.
• PT/INR is used to monitor oral anticoagulant therapy.
• Prothrombin time maybe prolonged in cases of chronic liver disease, vitamin K deficiency, disseminated
intravascular coagulation (DIC) and antiphospholipid antibody syndrome.
Interference in the assay can be caused by:
• Preanalytical errors such as hemolyzed, icteric, clotted specimens, improper blood-to-anticoagulant ratio and
lipemic samples (decreased prothrombin time).
• Contamination with saline, heparin, or other anticoagulants.
• Polycythemia with a hematocrit greater than 55%.
Reference: Yang R, Zubair M, Moosavi L. Prothrombin Time. [Updated 2024 Jan 23]. In: StatPearls [Internet]. Treasure
Island (FL): StatPearls Publishing; 2024 Jan. Available from: https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK544269.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
C-Reactive Protein [CRP]
mg/dL < 0.5 5.34
(Serum,Immunoturbidimetric)
CRP:
C-reactive protein (CRP) is one of the most sensitive acute-phase reactants for inflammation. CRP elevations are nonspecific
and may be useful for the detection of systemic inflammatory processes; to assess treatment of bacterial infections with
antibiotics; to detect intrauterine infections with concomitant premature amniorrhexis; to differentiate between active and
inactive forms of disease with concurrent infection; to therapeutically monitor rheumatic disease and assess anti-
inflammatory therapy; to determine the presence of postoperative complications at an early stage and to distinguish between
infection and bone marrow rejection.
```

```
BUN mg/dL 8-23 28.36
Urea mg/dL 16.6-48.5 60.70
Urea:
Urea is the final degradation product of protein and amino acid metabolism. Blood urea nitrogen currently is the most widely
used screening test for the evaluation of kidney function. Protein catabolism causes formation of ammonia which is
synthesized to urea with and elimination of excess nitrogen in the liver. Increased blood urea nitrogen may be due to cardiac
decompensation, water depletion due to decreased intake and excessive loss, increased protein catabolism, high protein
diet, acute glomerulonephritis, chronic nephritis, polycystic kidney disease, nephrosclerosis, tubular necrosis and all types of
obstruction of the urinary tract.
DDRR.. KKSSHHAAMMAA PPIIMMPPAALLGGAAOONNKKAARR DR. TALATNOOR SHEIKH DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
MM DD BBiioocchheemmiissttrryy MD PATHOLOGY M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
```

```
Potassium:
• Potassium: is the major intracellular cation and is critical to neural and muscle cell activity. Some causes of
decreased potassium levels include reduced intake of dietary potassium or excessive loss of potassium from the
body due to diarrhea, prolonged vomiting or increased renal excretion.Increased potassium levels may be caused by
dehydration or shock, severe burns, diabetic ketoacidosis, and retention of potassium by the kidney.
Blood Gas Analysis:
Blood gases are a group of tests that are performed together to measure the pH, the amount of oxygen and carbon dioxide
present in arterial blood in order to evaluate lung function and help detect an acid-base imbalance that could indicate a
respiratory, metabolic or kidney disorder.
```

```
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Coagulation Profile
Fibrinogen
(Citrate Plasma,Clauss Method)
Fibrinogen mg/dl 200-400 331.00
Test performed on Fully Automated Coagulometer.
Fibrinogen:
Fibrinogen is a blood plasma protein that is produced in the liver and is responsible for normal blood clotting.
Fibrinogen is an acute phase reactant.
High levels of fibrinogen are associated with an increased risk for cardiovascular disease.
Increased levels are also found during pregnancy, oral contraceptive use, inflammatory disorders (like rheumatoid arthritis
and glomerulonephritis), trauma, acute infections and certain cancers.
Acutely low levels are seen in:
• DIC
• Abnormal Fibrinolysis
• Rapid, large volume blood transfusions
Chronically low levels are seen in:
• Inherited conditions - afibrinogenemia hypofibrinogenemia
• Acquired conditions - End stage liver disease, severe malnutrition
∞ End of Report ∞
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Blood Urea Nitrogen
(Serum,Urease/Glutamate dehydrogenase)
BUN mg/dL 8-23 32.20
Urea mg/dL 16.6-48.5 68.90
Urea:
Urea is the final degradation product of protein and amino acid metabolism. Blood urea nitrogen currently is the most widely
used screening test for the evaluation of kidney function. Protein catabolism causes formation of ammonia which is
synthesized to urea with and elimination of excess nitrogen in the liver. Increased blood urea nitrogen may be due to cardiac
decompensation, water depletion due to decreased intake and excessive loss, increased protein catabolism, high protein
diet, acute glomerulonephritis, chronic nephritis, polycystic kidney disease, nephrosclerosis, tubular necrosis and all types of
obstruction of the urinary tract.
```

```
Method/ Principle of BacTAlert Virtuo analyser: BacT/ALERT Virtuo Microbial Detection Systems utilize a colorimetric
sensor and reflected light to monitor the presence and production of carbon dioxide (CO2) that is dissolved in the culture
medium. If microorganisms are present in the test sample, carbon dioxide is produced as the organisms metabolize the
substrates in the culture medium. When growth of the microorganisms produces CO2, the color of the gas-permeable sensor
installed in the bottom of each culture bottle changes to yellow. Neutralizes all classes of antibiotics by FAN Plus method that
normally hinder growth in manual blood culture methods.
Positive flagged cultures are processed on culture media. Identification by automated MALDITOF/Vitek 2 and or conventional
methods, sensitivity on vitek 2. Certain antibiotics tested by Kirby Bauer’s method and MIC is not reported for antibiotics
which are deduced by software as per CLSI. Antisera tested as and when applicable.
Remark:
1. Results of culture and antimicrobial susceptibility test needs to be correlate clinically.
2. Previous history of antibiotic usage may influence the growth of microorganisms in vitro.
Colony Count Interpretation
Colony Counts of 10000 to >= 100000 CFU/ml Significant uropathogen. Suggestive of Urinary
of single/two Potential pathogen/s. tract infection (UTI) needs treatment based on
antimicrobial susceptibility test results.
Colony counts between 1000 to 10000 Can be considered Significant growth,
CFU/ml of single Potential pathogen. correlation with Microscopy and Clinical
history required.
Colony counts between 100 to1000 CFU/ml. Insignificant growth. Probable commensal
contamination during voiding.
Either two or three organism types with Suggestive of Urinary tract infection (UTI)
predominant growth of one organism type and needs treatment based on antimicrobial
<10000CFU/mL of the other organism type(s) susceptibility test results. Correlation with
Microscopy and clinical history required
Any number / Any count. Significant in case of Suprapubic

urine specimens.
>= 3 organism types with no predominant Fresh specimen required as possibility of
```

```
Test performed on Fully Automated Coagulometer.
Prothrombin Time (PT):
• Prothrombin time (PT) is used to evaluate the extrinsic and common pathways of coagulation, which helps detect
deficiencies of factors ( II, V, VII, X ) and low fibrinogen concentrations.
• PT/INR is used to monitor oral anticoagulant therapy.
• Prothrombin time maybe prolonged in cases of chronic liver disease, vitamin K deficiency, disseminated
intravascular coagulation (DIC) and antiphospholipid antibody syndrome.
Interference in the assay can be caused by:
• Preanalytical errors such as hemolyzed, icteric, clotted specimens, improper blood-to-anticoagulant ratio and
lipemic samples (decreased prothrombin time).
• Contamination with saline, heparin, or other anticoagulants.
• Polycythemia with a hematocrit greater than 55%.
Reference: Yang R, Zubair M, Moosavi L. Prothrombin Time. [Updated 2024 Jan 23]. In: StatPearls [Internet]. Treasure
Island (FL): StatPearls Publishing; 2024 Jan. Available from: https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK544269.
```

```
Activated Partial Thromboplastin Time (APTT)

30.3
(Citrate Plasma)
APTT Ratio
1.15
(Citrate Plasma,Calculated)
APTT:
The activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT) test measures the functionality of the intrinsic and common pathways of the
coagulation cascade. (factors XII, XI, IX, VIII, X, V, II and Fibrinogen).
Prolonged APTT tests may be due to:
• Inherited or acquired factor deficiencies.
• A nonspecific inhibitor such as the lupus anticoagulant (LA)
• Specific inhibitor: Antibodies that attack a particular factor.
• DIC, Fibrinolysis
Interference in APTT:
Preanalytical variables such as Insufficient/ excess sample, Heparin contamination from IV lines, Clotted blood samples,
High hematocrit levels.
∞ End of Report ∞
DDRR.. AARRCCHHAANNAA VVAAZZIIFFDDAARR DR. PREETI SINGH
```

```
CRP:
C-reactive protein (CRP) is one of the most sensitive acute-phase reactants for inflammation. CRP elevations are nonspecific
and may be useful for the detection of systemic inflammatory processes; to assess treatment of bacterial infections with
antibiotics; to detect intrauterine infections with concomitant premature amniorrhexis; to differentiate between active and
inactive forms of disease with concurrent infection; to therapeutically monitor rheumatic disease and assess anti-
inflammatory therapy; to determine the presence of postoperative complications at an early stage and to distinguish between
infection and bone marrow rejection.
```

# Human Immunodeficiency Virus Ag/Ab

- **Date performed**: 2026-03-25

```
HIV Ag/ Ab Non-reactive,0.06 S/CO Non-Reactive: < 1.0

Human Immunodeficiency Virus Ag/Ab:
• This is a screening test for Human immunodeficiency virus (HIV) infection.
• HIV Ag/Ab CMIA result does not distinguish between the detection of HIV p24 antigen, HIV-1 antibody, or HIV-2
antibody reactivity.
• Antibody detection will be negative during window period.
• Testing & reporting is as per NACO guidelines.
• False positive results are seen in autoimmune disease, alcoholic hepatitis, primary billiary cirrhosis, leprosy, multiple
pregnancy.
• Antibody detection tests are not useful in children < 18 months as maternal antibodies may be present.
• All Positive/ Indeterminate tests should be confirmed by Western Blot/PCR assay.
• In case of Indeterminate results, patient should follow up for repeat testing after 3 months.
• The report should be handed over to patient / legally authorized representative (in case of Minor, unconscious,
mentally ill person) only after post-test counselling.
∞ End of Report ∞
```

## Verbatim text from PDF

```
Name : Saroj Agarwal Age/Gender:63 y / F Collected :25/03/2026 11:50
```

```
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Troponin I hs
pg/mL <= 15.6 11.90
(Serum,CMIA)
Troponin I hs:
Troponin is a complex that regulates the contraction of striated muscle. It consists of 3 subunits (C, T, and I). Troponin I is an
inhibitory protein and exhibits in 3 isoforms: cardiac muscle, slow-twitch skeletal muscle, and fast-twitch skeletal muscle. The
cardiac specificity of this isoform improves the accuracy of diagnosis in patients with acute or chronic skeletal muscle injury
and possible concomitant myocardial injury. Troponin I is released into the bloodstream within hours of the onset of
symptoms of myocardial infarction or ischemic damage. It can be detected at 3 to 6 hours following onset of chest pain with
peak concentrations at 12 to 16 hours, and remains elevated for 5 to 9 days. A positive troponin result is not always indicative
of myocardial infarction. Other conditions resulting in myocardial cell damage can contribute to elevated cardiac troponin I
levels. These conditions include, but are not limited to, myocarditis, cardiac surgery, angina, unstable angina, congestive
heart failure and noncardiac-related causes, such as, renal failure and pulmonary embolism.
DDRR.. KKSSHHAAMMAA PPIIMMPPAALLGGAAOONNKKAARR DR. TALATNOOR SHEIKH DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
MM DD BBiioocchheemmiissttrryy MD PATHOLOGY M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
CCoonnssuullttaanntt BBiioocchheemmiisstt Senior Clinical Associate Consultant Pathologist
```

```
NT pro B-type Natriuretic Peptide [NT
pro BNP] pg /mL 0-125 4089.00
(Serum,Electrochemiluminescence)
NT pro BNP:
1. B-type natriuretic peptide regulates blood pressure and fluid balance; is released in response to ventricle volume
expansion and/or pressure overload and is a marker of atrial and ventricular distension.
2. Concentrations increase with the severity of congestive heart failure. Lack of NT-proBNP elevations have been reported if
congestive heart failure is very acute or occurs with ventricular inflow obstruction.
3. Reported results are for the information of the referring Clinician. Results should be interpreted in correlation with medical
history, clinical presentation and other findings.
4. Reference ranges and clinical information/interpretations are traceable to kit inserts/textbooks/defined guidelines
```

```
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- BBIIOOCCHHEEMMIISSTTRRYY
Urea:
Urea is the final degradation product of protein and amino acid metabolism. Blood urea nitrogen currently is the most widely
used screening test for the evaluation of kidney function. Protein catabolism causes formation of ammonia which is
synthesized to urea with and elimination of excess nitrogen in the liver. Increased blood urea nitrogen may be due to cardiac
decompensation, water depletion due to decreased intake and excessive loss, increased protein catabolism, high protein
diet, acute glomerulonephritis, chronic nephritis, polycystic kidney disease, nephrosclerosis, tubular necrosis and all types of
obstruction of the urinary tract.
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
Consultant Biochemist Consultant Pathologist
```

```
Total Bilirubin:
• Diseases or conditions which, through hemolytic processes, produce bilirubin faster than the liver can metabolize it,
cause the levels of unconjugated (indirect) bilirubin to increase in the circulation.
• Liver immaturity and several other diseases in which the bilirubin conjugation mechanism is impaired cause similar
elevations of circulating unconjugated bilirubin.
• Bile duct obstruction or damage to hepatocellular structure causes increases in the levels of both conjugated (direct)
and unconjugated (indirect)bilirubin in the circulation.
```

## Summary (extracted)

2 DIMENSIONAL ECHOCARDIOGRAPHY & COLOUR DOPPLER STUDY
 Strong suspicion of pulmonary embolism. Large saddle shaped thrombus
noted at the bifurcation of RPA and LPA.
 Severe pulmonary hypertension. Moderate to severe TR, RVSP: 91mmHg.
PAT~ 91 msec.
 Dilated RA (40mm) and RV (50x45x77mm). E/o RV systolic dysfunction.
FAC: 20%
 Normal sized LV with septal flattening and good contractility. Overall LVEF :
60%.
• No e/o LV regional wall motion abnormality.
• Mild LV diastolic dysfunction (E/E’: 6).
• Structurally normal valves.
• Normal LA dimensions.
• Intact IAS and IVS.
• Normal IVC (16mm) with > 50% collapse with inspiration.
• No e/o pericardial effusion/vegetation.

> **Report 69 of 188** · `2026-03-24_CT_CT-Angiography-Pulmonary.md`

# CT Angiography - Pulmonary

- **Date performed**: 2026-03-24
- **Category**: CT
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-03-24_CT_CT-Angiography-Pulmonary.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-03-24_CT_CT-Angiography-Pulmonary.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_MED000000000000001004233620501000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

CT Angiography - Pulmonary
Technique: CT Pulmonary Angiography was performed following bolus tracking after
intravenous administration of 40ml of contrast. Sagittal and coronal reformatted and MIP
images were obtained.
Clinical details: Patient developed breathlessness and cough since 2-3 days. Developed
hypoxia yesterday.
Findings:
Pulmonary arteries are dilated. The pulmonary trunk measures 35 mm. The right pulmonary
artery measures 25 mm and left pulmonary artery measures 25 mm in calibre.
A saddle thrombus is seen extending from the main pulmonary trunk into the right and left
main pulmonary artery branches.
On the left side, the filling defect is further seen extending into the upper and lower lobar
segmental and subsegmental branches. Completely occluding thrombus is noted in proximal
left upper lobar segmental branch;
Partially obstructive filling defects are seen in the right distal pulmonary artery, segmental
and sub-segmental arterial branches of superior and all the basal segments [anterior,
medial, posterior, lateral] of right lower lobe; Partially obstructive filling defects in all
segmental and sub-segmental arterial branches of right middle and sub-segmental branches
of right upper lobe.
Bilateral moderate pleural effusion is seen with partial subsegmental collapse of both lower
lobes and lingular segment.
The visualised lung parenchyma reveals mosaic attenuation.
The right atrium and ventricle is mildly dilated. The interventricular septum is straight.
Visualized abdomen shows, two non-enhancing hypodense lesions noted in the right lobe of
liver, largest ~3.2 x 2.8 cm with lobulated margins- benign in aetiology. Mild perisplenic fluid
is noted. Tip of nasogastric tube is seen in duodenum.
1
Name : Saroj Agarwal Patient ID : 0010663186
Date of Birth : 27-08-1962 Age/Sex : 63 Years/F
Performing Date : 24-03-2026 06:42 PM Order No. : 0041235813
Referred By : Shah Darshit Report Date : 25-03-2026 11:03 AM
Study Description : CT Angiography - Pulmonary
Remarks
Acute submassive pulmonary embolism with saddle thrombus involving the main pulmonary
trunk into the right and left main pulmonary artery, lobar and segmental branches,
associated with RV strain and dilated pulmonary arteries- suggesting secondary pulmonary
hypertension.
Moderate bilateral pleural effusions with collapse of the underlying lung parenchyma.

```
Blood Gas Analysis:
Blood gases are a group of tests that are performed together to measure the pH, the amount of oxygen and carbon dioxide
present in arterial blood in order to evaluate lung function and help detect an acid-base imbalance that could indicate a
respiratory, metabolic or kidney disorder.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Creatinine:
Creatinine is synthesized endogenously from creatine and creatine phosphate and is removed from plasma by glomerular
filtration into the urine. Creatinine levels in renal disease generally do not increase until renal function is substantially
impaired.
```

S. Electrolytes (collected 10/03/2026 03:08, IP, Dr. Darshit Shah; Serum, Ion-selective electrode). Results: Sodium 133.20 mmol/L (LOW; ref 136-145); Potassium 4.15 mmol/L (Normal; ref 3.5-5.1); Chloride 98.10 mmol/L (Normal; ref 98-107). Hyponatremia noted. ## Summary (extracted)

Prothrombin Time (PT) (collected 09/03/2026 03:04, IP, Dr. Darshit Shah; Citrate Plasma, Nephelometry, Fully Automated Coagulometer). Results: Prothrombin Time 11.9 sec (within ref 9.93-12.47); Mean Normal PT 11.2 sec; INR 1.06 (within ref 0.86-1.14). All values within normal range. Notes: PT evaluates extrinsic/common pathways of coagulation; PT/INR is used to monitor oral anticoagulant therapy; PT may be prolonged in chronic liver disease, vitamin K deficiency, DIC, and antiphospholipid antibody syndrome. Includes Trend Analysis & Graph section.

```
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- HHAAEEMMAATTOOLLOOGGYY
Test performed on Fully Automated Coagulometer.
Prothrombin Time (PT):
• Prothrombin time (PT) is used to evaluate the extrinsic and common pathways of coagulation, which helps detect
deficiencies of factors ( II, V, VII, X ) and low fibrinogen concentrations.
• PT/INR is used to monitor oral anticoagulant therapy.
• Prothrombin time maybe prolonged in cases of chronic liver disease, vitamin K deficiency, disseminated
intravascular coagulation (DIC) and antiphospholipid antibody syndrome.
Interference in the assay can be caused by:
• Preanalytical errors such as hemolyzed, icteric, clotted specimens, improper blood-to-anticoagulant ratio and
lipemic samples (decreased prothrombin time).
• Contamination with saline, heparin, or other anticoagulants.
• Polycythemia with a hematocrit greater than 55%.
Reference: Yang R, Zubair M, Moosavi L. Prothrombin Time. [Updated 2024 Jan 23]. In: StatPearls [Internet]. Treasure
Island (FL): StatPearls Publishing; 2024 Jan. Available from: https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK544269.
DR. ARCHANA VAZIFDAR DR. TALATNOOR SHEIKH DR. PREETI SINGH
M.D ( Pathology) MD PATHOLOGY M.D Pathology
Head Of Hematopathology Senior Clinical Associate Consultant Pathologist
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

# pANCA/MPO ELISA Less than 2.0 RU/ml Negative: < 20

- **Date performed**: 2026-03-08
- **Category**: Lab-Serol
- **Department**: IMMUNOLOGY
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-03-08_Lab-Serol_pANCA-MPO-ELISA-Less-than-2-0-RU-ml-Negative-20.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-03-08_Lab-Serol_pANCA-MPO-ELISA-Less-than-2-0-RU-ml-Negative-20.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_OTD000000000000001004206028702000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

pANCA/MPO ELISA (collected 08/03/2026 11:56, IP, Dr. Darshit Shah; Serum, ELISA). Result: Less than 2.0 RU/ml. Reference range: Negative < 20, Positive >= 20 RU/ml. Result is within negative range. Notes: ANCA is a screening test for autoimmune vasculitis including Wegener's granulomatosis (WG), microscopic polyangiitis (MPA), Churg-Strauss syndrome, or organ-limited variants. Antibodies to MPO produce the pANCA pattern; useful in diagnosis and monitoring inflammatory activity.

## Verbatim text from PDF

```
Name : Saroj Agarwal Age/Gender:63 y / F Collected :08/03/2026 11:56
Patient ID : 0010663186 Visit Type :IP Received : 08/03/2026 11:56
Referred By : Dr. Darshit Shah DOB :27/08/1962 Reported :09/03/2026 15:37
Accession : 2600053150 Location :1T05S`1TR0509`1TB0509`1ONCOMED
DEPARTMENT OF LABORATORY MEDICINE - IMMUNOLOGY
Test Name Result Units Biological Reference Range
pANCA/MPO ELISA Less than 2.0 RU/ml Negative: < 20
(Serum,ELISA) Positive: >= 20
pANCA/MPO Test Interpretation:
1. Negative result indicates that there is no detectable level of pANCA.
2. Positive result needs to be correlated clinically;
3. It is advisable to combine ANCA IFA testing with monospecific ELISA assays for pANCA - anti-proteinase3 (Anti-PR3) and
cANCA - myeloperoxidase (Anti-MPO) for complete evaluation.
pANCA/MPO Clinical Information:
1. Anti neutrophil cytoplasmic antibody (ANCA) is a screening test in suspected cases of autoimmune vasculitis including
Wegener's granulomatosis (WG), microscopic polyangiitis (MPA), C-S syndrome, or organ-limited variants such as pauci-
immune necrotizing glomerulonephritis, chronic inflammatory bowel disease, chronic liver disease, etc.
2. ANCA react with enzymes in the cytoplasmic granules of human neutrophils including proteinase 3 (PR3),
myeloperoxidase (MPO), elastase, cathepsin G and other target antigens. Antibodies to MPO produce the pANCA pattern.
The test helps in diagnosis and to monitor inflammatory activity.
3. The results of tests for autoantibodies including ANCA and specific autoantibodies are ancillary hence therapeutic
decisions to judge the disease activity or to determine the response to treatment based solely on ANCA titres are not
generally recommended. Reported results are for the information of the referring Clinician. Results should be interpreted in
correlation with medical history, clinical presentation and other findings.
4. Reference ranges and clinical information/interpretations are traceable to kit inserts/textbooks/defined guidelines and
""https://www.mayocliniclabs.com/test-catalog/index.html".
∞ End of Report ∞
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
Consultant Biochemist Consultant Pathologist
```

# Magnesium

- **Date performed**: 2026-03-08
- **Category**: Lab-Serol
- **Department**: IMMUNOLOGY
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-03-08_Lab-Serol_Magnesium.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-03-08_Lab-Serol_Magnesium.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_OTD000000000000001004204820901000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

Magnesium (collected 08/03/2026 15:57, IP, Dr. Darshit Shah; Serum, Colorimetric Endpoint Method). Result: 2.21 mg/dL — within reference range 1.6-2.4 mg/dL (Normal/High borderline). Notes: Magnesium is a major intracellular cation and enzyme cofactor; ~70% stored in bone; regulated mainly via kidneys. Hypermagnesemia seen in renal failure; hypomagnesemia associated with alcoholism, malabsorption, pancreatitis, hypothyroidism, etc. Includes Trend Analysis & Graph section.

## Verbatim text from PDF

```
Name : Saroj Agarwal Age/Gender:63 y / F Collected :08/03/2026 15:57
Patient ID : 0010663186 Visit Type :IP Received : 08/03/2026 17:20
Referred By : Dr. Darshit Shah DOB :27/08/1962 Reported :08/03/2026 19:01
Accession : 2600053233 Location :1T05S`1TR0509`1TB0509`1ONCOMED
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- IIMMMMUUNNOOLLOOGGYY
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Magnesium
mg/dL 1.6-2.4 2.21
(Serum,Colorimetric Endpoint Method)
Magnesium:
Magnesium along with potassium is a major intracellular cation. Magnesium is a cofactor of many enzyme systems.
Approximately 70% of magnesium ions are stored in bone. Levels are regulated mainly via the kidneys. Hypermagnesemia is
found in acute and chronic renal failure, magnesium overload and magnesium release from the intracellular space related to
changes in calcium-, potassium- and phosphate-homeostasis. This may result in prolonged atrioventricular conduction time,
ventricular arrhythmias , coronary artery spasms, central nervous system depression or cardiac and/or respiratory arrest.
Conditions associated with hypomagnesemia include chronic alcoholism, childhood malnutrition, lactation, malabsorption,
acute pancreatitis, hypothyroidism, chronic glomerulonephritis, aldosteronism and prolonged intravenous feeding.
DDRR.. KKSSHHAAMMAA PPIIMMPPAALLGGAAOONNKKAARR DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
MM DD BBiioocchheemmiissttrryy M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
CCoonnssuullttaanntt BBiioocchheemmiisstt Consultant Pathologist
```

```
Test information:
The Anti-ENA Profile ELISA test kit provides a semiquantitative in vitro assay for human autoantibodies of the IgG class
against 8 different nuclear and cytoplasmic antigens.
1. Antinuclear antibody test is a sensitive test used to detect presence of specific autoantibodies. Antinuclear antibodies
occur in a variety of autoimmune diseases, both systemic and organ-specific.
2. The diagnosis is based primarily on the presence of compatible clinical signs and symptoms. The assay results for
autoantibodies are ancillary hence therapeutic decision, disease activity or response to treatment based solely on the result
values are not generally recommended.
3. Reported results are for the information of the referring Clinician. Results should be interpreted in correlation with medical
history, clinical presentation and other findings. Refer table for interpretation.
4. Reference ranges and clinical information/interpretations are traceable to kit inserts/textbooks/defined guidelines and
```

```
DEPARTMENT OF LABORATORY MEDICINE - IMMUNOLOGY
Test Name Result Units Biological Reference Range
Anti dsDNA ELISA IgG Less than 10.0 IU/ml Negative: < 100
(Serum,ELISA) Positive: >= 100
Anti dsDNA IgG:
1. Anti dsDNA antibodies are detectable in approximately 85% cases of SLE. Weakly-positive results caused by low-avidity
antibodies to dsDNA are not specific for SLE and can occur in a variety of diseases. Testing for these IgG antibodies is
indicated if ANA is positive along with clinical signs and symptoms compatible with SLE. If the ANA test is negative, test is
not advised.
2. Levels are known to fluctuate with disease activity in SLE, often increasing prior to an inflammation and decreasing in
response to therapy.
3. The assay results for autoantibodies are ancillary hence therapeutic decision, disease activity or response to treatment
based solely on result values are not generally recommended. Reported results are for the information of the referring
Clinician. Results should be interpreted in correlation with medical history, clinical presentation and other findings.
4. Reference ranges and clinical information/interpretations are traceable to kit inserts/textbooks/defined guidelines and
"https://www.mayocliniclabs.com/test-catalog/index.html".
```

```
ANA Test Interpretation:
1. Sample screening dilution is 1:100.
2. Negative result indicates that there is no detectable level of antinuclear antibodies.
3. Trace positive result needs to be correlated clinically; repeat test after 6 weeks; further testing for detection of
specific antigens / autoantibodies can be done.
4. Positive result needs to be correlated clinically; further testing for detection of specific antigens /
autoantibodies can be done.
5. Immunofluorescence pattern can indicate the antigen type and its clinical association.
ANA Clinical Information:
1. Antinuclear antibody test is a sensitive screening test used to detect presence of autoantibodies which occur
in a variety of autoimmune diseases, both systemic and organ-specific. The diagnosis is based primarily on the
presence of compatible clinical signs and symptoms.

treatment based solely on the result values are not generally recommended.

with medical history, clinical presentation and other findings.
```

# Troponin I hs Less than

- **Date performed**: 2026-03-08
- **Category**: Lab-Biochem
- **Department**: BIOCHEMISTRY
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-03-08_Lab-Biochem_Troponin-I-hs-Less-than.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-03-08_Lab-Biochem_Troponin-I-hs-Less-than.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_OTD000000000000001004204821001000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

Troponin I hs (Serum, CMIA): 3.2 pg/mL (Less than reference; Reference <= 15.6 pg/mL). Result is in the normal/low range.

Notes from report: Troponin I is a cardiac-specific marker released into the bloodstream within hours of myocardial infarction or ischemic damage; detectable at 3-6 hours after chest pain, peaks at 12-16 hours, remains elevated 5-9 days. Elevated levels can also occur with myocarditis, cardiac surgery, angina, unstable angina, CHF, renal failure, and pulmonary embolism.

## Verbatim text from PDF

```
Name : Saroj Agarwal Age/Gender:63 y / F Collected :08/03/2026 15:57
Patient ID : 0010663186 Visit Type :IP Received : 08/03/2026 17:20
Referred By : Dr. Darshit Shah DOB :27/08/1962 Reported :08/03/2026 19:01
Accession : 2600053233 Location :1T05S`1TR0509`1TB0509`1ONCOMED
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- BBIIOOCCHHEEMMIISSTTRRYY
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Troponin I hs Less than
pg/mL <= 15.6
(Serum,CMIA) 3.2
Troponin I hs:
Troponin is a complex that regulates the contraction of striated muscle. It consists of 3 subunits (C, T, and I). Troponin I is an
inhibitory protein and exhibits in 3 isoforms: cardiac muscle, slow-twitch skeletal muscle, and fast-twitch skeletal muscle. The
cardiac specificity of this isoform improves the accuracy of diagnosis in patients with acute or chronic skeletal muscle injury
and possible concomitant myocardial injury. Troponin I is released into the bloodstream within hours of the onset of
symptoms of myocardial infarction or ischemic damage. It can be detected at 3 to 6 hours following onset of chest pain with
peak concentrations at 12 to 16 hours, and remains elevated for 5 to 9 days. A positive troponin result is not always indicative
of myocardial infarction. Other conditions resulting in myocardial cell damage can contribute to elevated cardiac troponin I
levels. These conditions include, but are not limited to, myocarditis, cardiac surgery, angina, unstable angina, congestive
heart failure and noncardiac-related causes, such as, renal failure and pulmonary embolism.
∞ End of Report ∞
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Magnesium
mg/dL 1.6-2.4 2.21
(Serum,Colorimetric Endpoint Method)
Magnesium:
Magnesium along with potassium is a major intracellular cation. Magnesium is a cofactor of many enzyme systems.
Approximately 70% of magnesium ions are stored in bone. Levels are regulated mainly via the kidneys. Hypermagnesemia is
found in acute and chronic renal failure, magnesium overload and magnesium release from the intracellular space related to
changes in calcium-, potassium- and phosphate-homeostasis. This may result in prolonged atrioventricular conduction time,
ventricular arrhythmias , coronary artery spasms, central nervous system depression or cardiac and/or respiratory arrest.
Conditions associated with hypomagnesemia include chronic alcoholism, childhood malnutrition, lactation, malabsorption,
acute pancreatitis, hypothyroidism, chronic glomerulonephritis, aldosteronism and prolonged intravenous feeding.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some

and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

Creatinine:
```
Creatinine is synthesized endogenously from creatine and creatine phosphate and is removed from plasma by glomerular
filtration into the urine. Creatinine levels in renal disease generally do not increase until renal function is substantially
impaired.
```

## Summary (extracted)

Magnesium (Department of Laboratory Medicine - Immunology), collected 02/03/2026 10:39. Serum Magnesium (Colorimetric Endpoint Method) 2.39 mg/dL (within ref 1.6-2.4 — borderline high).

## Verbatim text from PDF

```
Name : Saroj Agarwal Age/Gender:63 y / F Collected :02/03/2026 10:39
Patient ID : 0010663186 Visit Type :IP Received : 02/03/2026 10:57
Referred By : Dr. Darshit Shah DOB :27/08/1962 Reported :02/03/2026 13:44
Accession : 2600048564 Location :1T05S`1TR0509`1TB0509`1ONCOMED
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- IIMMMMUUNNOOLLOOGGYY
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
Magnesium
mg/dL 1.6-2.4 2.39
(Serum,Colorimetric Endpoint Method)
Magnesium:
Magnesium along with potassium is a major intracellular cation. Magnesium is a cofactor of many enzyme systems.
Approximately 70% of magnesium ions are stored in bone. Levels are regulated mainly via the kidneys. Hypermagnesemia is
found in acute and chronic renal failure, magnesium overload and magnesium release from the intracellular space related to
changes in calcium-, potassium- and phosphate-homeostasis. This may result in prolonged atrioventricular conduction time,
ventricular arrhythmias , coronary artery spasms, central nervous system depression or cardiac and/or respiratory arrest.
Conditions associated with hypomagnesemia include chronic alcoholism, childhood malnutrition, lactation, malabsorption,
acute pancreatitis, hypothyroidism, chronic glomerulonephritis, aldosteronism and prolonged intravenous feeding.
∞ End of Report ∞
DDRR.. KKSSHHAAMMAA PPIIMMPPAALLGGAAOONNKKAARR DR. ARCHI CHAWLA DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
MM DD BBiioocchheemmiissttrryy M.D Pathology M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
CCoonnssuullttaanntt BBiioocchheemmiisstt Clinical Assistant Consultant Pathologist
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Potassium:
• Potassium: is the major intracellular cation and is critical to neural and muscle cell activity. Some causes of
decreased potassium levels include reduced intake of dietary potassium or excessive loss of potassium from the
body due to diarrhea, prolonged vomiting or increased renal excretion.Increased potassium levels may be caused by
dehydration or shock, severe burns, diabetic ketoacidosis, and retention of potassium by the kidney.
```

```
Sodium:
• Sodium: is the major extracellular cation and functions to maintain fluid distribution and osmotic pressure. Some
causes of decreased levels of sodium include prolonged vomiting or diarrhoea, diminished reabsorption in the kidney
and excessive fluid retention. Common causes of increased sodium include excessive fluid loss, high salt intake and
increased kidney reabsorption.
```

```
Potassium:
• Potassium: is the major intracellular cation and is critical to neural and muscle cell activity. Some causes of
decreased potassium levels include reduced intake of dietary potassium or excessive loss of potassium from the
body due to diarrhea, prolonged vomiting or increased renal excretion.Increased potassium levels may be caused by
dehydration or shock, severe burns, diabetic ketoacidosis, and retention of potassium by the kidney.
Blood Gas Analysis:
Blood gases are a group of tests that are performed together to measure the pH, the amount of oxygen and carbon dioxide
present in arterial blood in order to evaluate lung function and help detect an acid-base imbalance that could indicate a
respiratory, metabolic or kidney disorder.
```

```
Urea:
Urea is the final degradation product of protein and amino acid metabolism. Blood urea nitrogen currently is the most widely
used screening test for the evaluation of kidney function. Protein catabolism causes formation of ammonia which is
synthesized to urea with and elimination of excess nitrogen in the liver. Increased blood urea nitrogen may be due to cardiac
decompensation, water depletion due to decreased intake and excessive loss, increased protein catabolism, high protein
diet, acute glomerulonephritis, chronic nephritis, polycystic kidney disease, nephrosclerosis, tubular necrosis and all types of
obstruction of the urinary tract.
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. TALATNOOR SHEIKH DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry MD PATHOLOGY M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
Consultant Biochemist Senior Clinical Associate Consultant Pathologist
```

```
C-Reactive Protein [CRP]
mg/dL < 0.5 0.18
(Serum,Immunoturbidimetric)
CRP:
C-reactive protein (CRP) is one of the most sensitive acute-phase reactants for inflammation. CRP elevations are nonspecific
and may be useful for the detection of systemic inflammatory processes; to assess treatment of bacterial infections with
antibiotics; to detect intrauterine infections with concomitant premature amniorrhexis; to differentiate between active and
inactive forms of disease with concurrent infection; to therapeutically monitor rheumatic disease and assess anti-
inflammatory therapy; to determine the presence of postoperative complications at an early stage and to distinguish between
infection and bone marrow rejection.
```

```
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- BBIIOOCCHHEEMMIISSTTRRYY
Potassium:
• Potassium: is the major intracellular cation and is critical to neural and muscle cell activity. Some causes of
decreased potassium levels include reduced intake of dietary potassium or excessive loss of potassium from the
body due to diarrhea, prolonged vomiting or increased renal excretion.Increased potassium levels may be caused by
dehydration or shock, severe burns, diabetic ketoacidosis, and retention of potassium by the kidney.
Blood Gas Analysis:
Blood gases are a group of tests that are performed together to measure the pH, the amount of oxygen and carbon dioxide
present in arterial blood in order to evaluate lung function and help detect an acid-base imbalance that could indicate a
respiratory, metabolic or kidney disorder.
∞ End of Report ∞
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
Consultant Biochemist Consultant Pathologist
```

# USG Portable Single Organ

- **Date performed**: 2026-02-23
- **Category**: USG
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-02-23_USG_USG-Portable-Single-Organ.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-02-23_USG_USG-Portable-Single-Organ.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_MED000000000000001004182051500000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

USG Portable Single Organ — chest ultrasound performed at bedside (23-02-2026 13:33). Clinical profile: known operated case of CA uterus with bilateral pleural effusions, left-sided ICD placed; scan to evaluate status of pleural fluid and functioning of ICD. Portable ultrasound of chest performed using low frequency convex transducer.

Findings:
- Right costophrenic space: Mild right pleural effusion (approximate volume 150-200 cc) with underlying lung showing passive atelectasis with consolidation.
- Left costophrenic space: Mild, septated left pleural effusion (approximate volume 150-200 cc) with underlying lung showing passive atelectasis with consolidation. The previously placed ICD is anterior in location; its tip could not be well appreciated in this scan.
- Few lobulated pleural-based hypoechoic foci, largest measuring 3.7 x 2.4 cm, are seen along the base of the pleural cavity, likely representing metastatic deposits.

Remarks/Impression: Bilateral mild pleural effusions; septated on the left side with associated pleural deposits. Reported by Dr. Saba Shaikh (DMRD, DMRE, DNB; Visiting Consultant; MMC 87736).

```
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- BBIIOOCCHHEEMMIISSTTRRYY
Urea:
Urea is the final degradation product of protein and amino acid metabolism. Blood urea nitrogen currently is the most widely
used screening test for the evaluation of kidney function. Protein catabolism causes formation of ammonia which is
synthesized to urea with and elimination of excess nitrogen in the liver. Increased blood urea nitrogen may be due to cardiac
decompensation, water depletion due to decreased intake and excessive loss, increased protein catabolism, high protein
diet, acute glomerulonephritis, chronic nephritis, polycystic kidney disease, nephrosclerosis, tubular necrosis and all types of
obstruction of the urinary tract.
DR. KSHAMA PIMPALGAONKAR DR. ARCHI CHAWLA DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
M D Biochemistry M.D Pathology M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
Consultant Biochemist Clinical Assistant Consultant Pathologist
Page 3 of 8
Disclaimer: Tests marked with NABL symbol are accredited by NABL vide certificate number
```

# C-Reactive Protein [CRP]

- **Date performed**: 2026-02-23
- **Category**: Lab-Biochem
- **Department**: BIOCHEMISTRY
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-02-23_Lab-Biochem_C-Reactive-Protein-CRP.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-02-23_Lab-Biochem_C-Reactive-Protein-CRP.pdf)

## Summary (extracted)

C-Reactive Protein [CRP] (Serum, Immunoturbidimetric): 1.07 mg/dL (High; reference range <0.5 mg/dL). Elevated CRP indicates an acute-phase inflammatory response. Reported by Dr. Kshama Pimpalgaonkar, Dr. Archi Chawla, Dr. Srikant Gharpure.

```
Accession : 2600043130 Location :1T06N`1TR0601`1TB0605`1ONCOMED
DDEEPPAARRTTMMEENNTT OOFF LLAABBOORRAATTOORRYY MMEEDDIICCIINNEE -- BBIIOOCCHHEEMMIISSTTRRYY
Reference Low Normal High
Test Name Unit Range
C-Reactive Protein [CRP]
mg/dL < 0.5 1.07
(Serum,Immunoturbidimetric)
CRP:
C-reactive protein (CRP) is one of the most sensitive acute-phase reactants for inflammation. CRP elevations are nonspecific
and may be useful for the detection of systemic inflammatory processes; to assess treatment of bacterial infections with
antibiotics; to detect intrauterine infections with concomitant premature amniorrhexis; to differentiate between active and
inactive forms of disease with concurrent infection; to therapeutically monitor rheumatic disease and assess anti-
inflammatory therapy; to determine the presence of postoperative complications at an early stage and to distinguish between
infection and bone marrow rejection.
∞ End of Report ∞
DDRR.. KKSSHHAAMMAA PPIIMMPPAALLGGAAOONNKKAARR DR. ARCHI CHAWLA DR. SRIKANT GHARPURE
MM DD BBiioocchheemmiissttrryy M.D Pathology M.D, DPB, DCP (London)
```

# Urine Culture Colony Count

- **Date performed**: 2026-02-21
- **Category**: Lab-Micro
- **Department**: MICROBIOLOGY
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-02-21_Lab-Micro_Urine-Culture-Colony-Count.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-02-21_Lab-Micro_Urine-Culture-Colony-Count.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_OTD000000000000001004180139507000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

Urine Culture Colony Count (Foleys catheter sample, clinical details: CA endometrium). WET MOUNT microscopy: Pus cells 5-10/hpf, RBCs 65-70/hpf, Epithelial cells 0-5/hpf, Bacteria absent, Yeast — budding yeast cells with pseudohyphae seen. Culture grew two organisms: (1) Enterococcus faecium — Colony Count >10^5 CFU/mL (Significant bacteriuria); (2) Candida tropicalis — Colony Count >10^5 CFU/mL (Significant growth).

Drug susceptibility — Candida tropicalis (all Susceptible): Caspofungin <=0.12, Fluconazole 1.0, Micafungin <=0.06, Voriconazole <=0.12 µg/ml.

Drug susceptibility — Enterococcus faecium: Resistant to Benzylpenicillin (>=64), Ciprofloxacin (>=8), Levofloxacin (>=8), Nitrofurantoin (256), Ampicillin, Norfloxacin; Susceptible to Linezolid (2), Teicoplanin (<=0.5), Vancomycin (<=0.5), Tetracyclin (>=16); Susceptible-Dose dependent to Daptomycin (0.25). Comment notes Candida species is a common colonizer of indwelling urinary catheters; Voriconazole and Echinocandins poorly excreted in urine. Reported by Dr. Neetu Biyani and Dr. Shashikala Shivaprakasha.

```
Comment
Candida species is a colonizer of indwelling
urinary catheters, especially in patients on
broad spectrum antibiotics.
Kindly correlate clinically.
Voriconazole and Echinocandins are poorly
excreted in urine and should be avoided for
lower urinary tract infections.
Enterococcus faecium is inherently resistant to
Cephalosporins, Aminoglycosides,
Clindamycin, Trimethoprim, Trimethoprim-
sulfamethoxazole and Fusidic Acid. An
interpretation of susceptible for ampicillin in
beta- lactamase negative enterococci is also
applicable to amoxicillin- clavulanate,
ampicillin- sulbactam, piperacillin and
piperacillin- tazobactam among non-ß-
lactamase producing enterococci. Combination
therapy of ampicillin, penicillin, or vancomycin
(for susceptible strains) plus an
aminoglycoside, is usually indicated for serious
enterococcal infections, such as endocarditis,
unless resistance to both high- level
gentamicin and high- level streptomycin is
documented; such combinations are predicted
to result in synergistic killing of enterococcus.

1. Result of culture and antimicrobial susceptibility test need to be correlated clinically.
2. Previous history of antibiotic usage may influence the growth of microorganisms in vitro.
3. Sterile pyuria is a condition in which the pus cells/ white cells are present in the urine without bacterial infection.
4. Asymptomatic bacteriuria, is a condition in which bacterial count may be significant but patient does not experience
any symptoms.
Colony Count Interpretation
Colony Counts of 10000 to >= 100000 CFU/ml Significant uropathogen. Suggestive of Urinary
of single/two Potential pathogen/s. tract infection (UTI) needs treatment based on
antimicrobial susceptibility test results.
Colony counts between 1000 to 10000 Can be considered Significant growth,
CFU/ml of single Potential pathogen. correlation with Microscopy and Clinical
history required.
Colony counts between 100 to1000 CFU/ml. Insignificant growth. Probable commensal
contamination during voiding.
Either two or three organism types with Suggestive of Urinary tract infection (UTI)
predominant growth of one organism type and needs treatment based on antimicrobial
<10000CFU/mL of the other organism type(s) susceptibility test results. Correlation with
Microscopy and clinical history required
Any number / Any count. Significant in case of Suprapubic
aspirates/surgically obtained (e.g. cystoscopy)
urine specimens.
>= 3 organism types with no predominant Fresh specimen required as possibility of
(10000 >= 100000 CFU/ml) pathogen. contamination during voiding.
```

```
Test Name Result
Sputum Culture:
Interpretation for Sputum specimen only:
Grading of AFB smear by Z-N- Stain on basis of NTEP/WHO (National Tuberculosis Elimination Programme/ World Health
Organisation) recommendation.
Examination finding No. of fields examined Grading Result
No AFB in 100 oil immersion 100 0 Negative
fields
1-9 AFB per 100 oil immersion 100 Scanty* Positive
fields
10-99 AFB per 100 oil 100 1+ Positive
immersion fields
1-10 AFB per oil immersion field 50 2+ Positive
More than 10 AFB per oil 20 3+ Positive
Immersion field
*Record actual number of bacilli seen in 100 fields – e.g. “Scanty 4"
Method: Specimen processed on culture media. Identification by automated MALDITOF / Vitek2 & or conventional methods, sensitivity on Vitek 2 Certain
antibiotics tested by Kirby Bauer’s method and MIC value is not reported for antibiotics which are deduced by software as per CLSI Guidelines. Colistin MIC
is tested by Microbroth Dilution method.
Remarks:
• Results of culture and antimicrobial susceptibility test needs to be correlate clinically.
• Previous history of antibiotic usage may influence the growth of microorganisms in vitro.
• Result is dependent on the quality of specimen submitted.
• Smear-positivity and grade indicates relative bacterial burden.
• Changes in smear status important for monitoring response to therapy.
• Kindly note AFB stain does not distinguish between viable and dead organisms nor differentiates species of Mycobacteria.
• Mycobacteria Genxpert and MTB automated culture recommended if clinically indicated.
• A negative AFB smear may mean that no infection is present, that symptoms are caused by some other microorganism, or that the mycobacteria
were not present in sufficient numbers to be seen under the microscope.
```

# WB FDG PET - CECT scan

- **Date performed**: 2026-02-21
- **Category**: CT
- **Source PDF**: [`./report_pdf/2026-02-21_CT_WB-FDG-PET-CECT-scan.pdf`](./report_pdf/2026-02-21_CT_WB-FDG-PET-CECT-scan.pdf)
- **Original filename**: `MedicalReport_MED000000000000001004179439600000.pdf`

## Summary (extracted)

18F-FDG WB PET-CT Scan
Clinical History: 63-year-old female, presented with complaints of breathlessness,
productive cough, bilateral pedal edema for the past 2 months; persisting hematuria since
12/02/26. Chest X Ray showed left sided pleural effusion. ICD was inserted (12/02/26),
pleural fluid cytology revealed clusters of atypical cells suggestive of carcinoma with large
cell morphology. CT Chest + Abdomen (13/02/26): Bilateral pleural effusion with left sided
enhancing pleural thickening, hyperenhancing nodule in segment VIII of liver. She received
C #1 Pacliqualip + Carboplatin (20/02/26- Day 1). Patient has a history of Carcinoma
endometrium, operated 3 years ago. Scan for disease status assessment.
Labs (20/02/26): TLC – 13.88 (Neutrophil – 89.3%); INR – 2.4
Urine Routine (20/02/26): Pus cells - >100/hpf; RBC - >100/hpf; Bacteria - Present
Technique: 7.28mCi of 18F-FDG was injected intravenously and PET-CT scan was acquired from
vertex to mid-thigh after one hour. Contrast-enhanced CT scan was performed as part of the PET-
CT protocol. Breath-hold CT of the lungs was acquired as well. Standardized uptake values (SUV)
were calculated based on body weight.
FINDINGS:
Excessive motion artefacts seen- suboptimal assessment.
Brain:
Normal distribution of metabolic activity is noted intracranially. No focal area of abnormal
increased tracer avid definite lesion seen. Tiny gliotic foci seen in right ganglio-capsular
region - sequelae to ischemic insult.
Head & Neck:
Nasopharynx and hypopharynx are unremarkable.
Localized linearly increased FDG uptake is seen along the minor salivary glands in right
cheek – SUVmax 7.7 - ? inflammatory.
Intense FDG uptake noted along the inner surface of buccal mucosa- right greater than left
- SUVmax 13.85: Likely excessive physiological simulation/inflammatory.
Thyroid appears normal in size and shows no abnormal tracer uptake.
Moderate to high grade FDG avid left cervical level II, III, IV and V partly necrotic nodes
are seen. Largest - left VC node measures 2 x 2.4 cm, SUVmax 12.74
